{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01AGV4disFWuj85nLbUzaKae","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# apiserver Architecture\n     2→\n     3→## 1. Server Composition\n     4→\n     5→The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n     6→`GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\n     7→layer.\n     8→\n     9→This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\n    10→flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\n    11→populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\n    12→instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\n    13→function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\n    14→\n    15→```mermaid\n    16→graph TD\n    17→    subgraph Incoming Request\n    18→        direction LR\n    19→        A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n    20→    end\n    21→\n    22→    subgraph kube-apiserver process\n    23→        direction LR\n    24→        B --> C[Aggregator Server];\n    25→        C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\n    26→        D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\n    27→        C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\n    28→        D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\n    29→        G -- Handles CRD --> E;\n    30→    end\n    31→```\n    32→\n    33→1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\n    34→    *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\n    35→        extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\n    36→        \"aggregated\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\n    37→    *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\n    38→        `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \"claimed\"\n    39→        that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\n    40→        `Service` and proxies the request.\n    41→    *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\n    42→        custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\n    43→        storage backends.\n    44→    *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\n    45→        server in the chain.\n    46→\n    47→2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\n    48→    *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\n    49→    *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\n    50→        strategies.\n    51→    *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\n    52→        it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\n    53→\n    54→3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\n    55→    *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\n    56→        `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\n    57→        mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\n    58→        documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\n    59→    *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\n    60→        new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\n    61→    *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\n    62→        schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\n    63→        custom API server code.\n    64→    *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\n    65→        Found` is returned.\n    66→\n    67→## 2. Handler Chain\n    68→\n    69→Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\n    70→is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\n    71→chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\n    72→`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\n    73→\n    74→```mermaid\n    75→sequenceDiagram\n    76→    participant Client\n    77→    participant Handler Chain\n    78→    participant Authentication\n    79→    participant Authorization\n    80→    participant Priority and Fairness\n    81→    participant Admission Control\n    82→    participant REST Endpoint\n    83→\n    84→    Client->>Handler Chain: Request\n    85→    Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\n    86→    Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\n    87→    Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\n    88→    Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\n    89→    Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\n    90→    Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\n    91→    Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\n    92→    Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\n    93→    Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\n    94→    REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\n    95→    Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\n    96→```\n    97→\n    98→The handler chain consists of the following stages:\n    99→\n   100→1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\n   101→    pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n   102→    The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n   103→    identifies the user.\n   104→2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n   105→    perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n   106→    (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n   107→    If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n   108→3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n   109→    concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n   110→    overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n   111→    server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n   112→4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n   113→    enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n   114→    object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n   115→    Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n   116→    at the namespace level.\n   117→5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n   118→    appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n   119→\n   120→## 3. API Group Registration\n   121→\n   122→The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n   123→\n   124→1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n   125→2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n   126→    boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n   127→3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n   128→    resource in its `Strategy` object.\n   129→4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n   130→    `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n   131→    method.\n   132→\n   133→### The API Group Registry\n   134→\n   135→The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n   136→`Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\n   137→capabilities:\n   138→\n   139→*   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n   140→    (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\n   141→    tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\n   142→    objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\n   143→\n   144→*   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\n   145→    between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\n   146→    `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n   147→\n   148→*   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n   149→    an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n   150→\n   151→*   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n   152→    functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\n   153→    handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\n   154→\n   155→### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\n   156→\n   157→With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\n   158→the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\n   159→\n   160→```mermaid\n   161→graph TD\n   162→    subgraph Server Configuration\n   163→        A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\n   164→        A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\n   165→        A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\n   166→        A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\n   167→    end\n   168→\n   169→    subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\n   170→        C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\n   171→        E --> F[etcd client];\n   172→        E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\n   173→    end\n   174→\n   175→    subgraph Server Runtime\n   176→        H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\n   177→        I -- Uses --> A;\n   178→        I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n   179→        J --> K[HTTP Handler];\n   180→        K -- On Request --> C;\n   181→    end\n   182→```\n   183→\n   184→The registration process follows these steps:\n   185→\n   186→1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\n   187→    which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\n   188→    implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\n   189→\n   190→2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\n   191→    is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\n   192→    logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\n   193→\n   194→3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\n   195→    `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\n   196→\n   197→## 4. Watch Cache\n   198→\n   199→To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\n   200→apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\n   201→`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\n   202→\n   203→*   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\n   204→    objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\n   205→    that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\n   206→*   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\n   207→    dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\n   208→    cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\n   209→    etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent—waiting for it to\n   210→    refresh if necessary—before serving the request.\n   211→*   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\n   212→    cache's buffer, the request \"falls through\" to the underlying etcd storage.\n   213→*   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\n   214→    unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\n   215→    which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\n   216→    not been modified.\n   217→\n   218→## 5. Conflict Resolution\n   219→\n   220→*   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\n   221→    read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\n   222→    object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\n   223→    it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\n   224→    update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\n   225→    modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\n   226→    `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\n   227→    forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\n   228→    `resourceVersion`.\n   229→*   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \"intent-based\" patch. The server maintains a\n   230→    `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \"manager\" (e.g., a\n   231→    controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\n   232→    same object without overwriting each other's changes.\n   233→\n   234→## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\n   235→\n   236→Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\n   237→specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\n   238→\n   239→*   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\n   240→    validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\n   241→*   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\n   242→    `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\n   243→*   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\n   244→    JSON spec that it serves to clients.\n   245→\n   246→## 7. Security & Observability\n   247→\n   248→*   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\n   249→    policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\n   250→*   **Security:**\n   251→    *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\n   252→    *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\n   253→        issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\n   254→\n   255→## 8. Streaming Protocols\n   256→\n   257→*   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\n   258→    connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\n   259→    `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\n   260→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Server Composition\n\nThe `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n`GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\nlayer.\n\nThis composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\nflags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\npopulate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\ninstances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\nfunction in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Incoming Request\n        direction LR\n        A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n    end\n\n    subgraph kube-apiserver process\n        direction LR\n        B --> C[Aggregator Server];\n        C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\n        D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\n        C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\n        D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\n        G -- Handles CRD --> E;\n    end\n```\n\n1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\n    *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\n        extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\n        \"aggregated\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\n    *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\n        `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \"claimed\"\n        that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\n        `Service` and proxies the request.\n    *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\n        custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\n        storage backends.\n    *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\n        server in the chain.\n\n2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\n    *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\n    *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\n        strategies.\n    *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\n        it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\n\n3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\n    *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\n        `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\n        mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\n        documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\n    *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\n        new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\n    *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\n        schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\n        custom API server code.\n    *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\n        Found` is returned.\n\n## 2. Handler Chain\n\nEvery request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\nis not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\nchain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant Client\n    participant Handler Chain\n    participant Authentication\n    participant Authorization\n    participant Priority and Fairness\n    participant Admission Control\n    participant REST Endpoint\n\n    Client->>Handler Chain: Request\n    Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\n    Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\n    Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\n    Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\n    Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\n    Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\n    Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\n    Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\n    Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\n    REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\n    Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\n```\n\nThe handler chain consists of the following stages:\n\n1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\n    pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n    The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n    identifies the user.\n2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n    perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n    (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n    If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n    concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n    overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n    server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n    enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n    object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n    Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n    at the namespace level.\n5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n    appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n\n## 3. API Group Registration\n\nThe high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n\n1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n    boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n    resource in its `Strategy` object.\n4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n    `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n    method.\n\n### The API Group Registry\n\nThe `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n`Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\ncapabilities:\n\n*   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n    (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\n    tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\n    objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\n\n*   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\n    between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\n    `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n\n*   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n    an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n\n*   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n    functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\n    handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\n\n### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\n\nWith a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\nthe `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph Server Configuration\n        A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\n        A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\n        A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\n        A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\n    end\n\n    subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\n        C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\n        E --> F[etcd client];\n        E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\n    end\n\n    subgraph Server Runtime\n        H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\n        I -- Uses --> A;\n        I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n        J --> K[HTTP Handler];\n        K -- On Request --> C;\n    end\n```\n\nThe registration process follows these steps:\n\n1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\n    which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\n    implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\n\n2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\n    is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\n    logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\n\n3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\n    `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\n\n## 4. Watch Cache\n\nTo handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\napiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\n\n*   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\n    objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\n    that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\n*   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\n    dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\n    cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\n    etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent—waiting for it to\n    refresh if necessary—before serving the request.\n*   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\n    cache's buffer, the request \"falls through\" to the underlying etcd storage.\n*   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\n    unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\n    which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\n    not been modified.\n\n## 5. Conflict Resolution\n\n*   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\n    read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\n    object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\n    it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\n    update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\n    modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\n    `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\n    forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\n    `resourceVersion`.\n*   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \"intent-based\" patch. The server maintains a\n    `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \"manager\" (e.g., a\n    controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\n    same object without overwriting each other's changes.\n\n## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\n\nApiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\nspecifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\n\n*   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\n    validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\n*   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\n    `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\n*   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\n    JSON spec that it serves to clients.\n\n## 7. Security & Observability\n\n*   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\n    policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\n*   **Security:**\n    *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\n    *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\n        issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\n\n## 8. Streaming Protocols\n\n*   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\n    connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\n    `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\n","numLines":260,"startLine":1,"totalLines":260}}}

It is expected\n    55→// that objects may implement any of the below interfaces.\n    56→//\n    57→// Consider using StorageWithReadiness whenever possible.\n    58→type Storage interface {\n    59→\t// New returns an empty object that can be used with Create and Update after request data has been put into it.\n    60→\t// This object must be a pointer type for use with Codec.DecodeInto([]byte, runtime.Object)\n    61→\tNew() runtime.Object\n    62→\n    63→\t// Destroy cleans up its resources on shutdown.\n    64→\t// Destroy has to be implemented in thread-safe way and be prepared\n    65→\t// for being called more than once.\n    66→\tDestroy()\n    67→}\n    68→\n    69→// StorageWithReadiness extends Storage interface with the readiness check.\n    70→type StorageWithReadiness interface {\n    71→\tStorage\n    72→\n    73→\t// ReadinessCheck allows for checking storage readiness.\n    74→\tReadinessCheck() error\n    75→}\n    76→\n    77→// Scoper indicates what scope the resource is at. It must be specified.\n    78→// It is usually provided automatically based on your strategy.\n    79→type Scoper interface {\n    80→\t// NamespaceScoped returns true if the storage is namespaced\n    81→\tNamespaceScoped() bool\n    82→}\n    83→\n    84→// KindProvider specifies a different kind for its API than for its internal storage.  This is necessary for external\n    85→// objects that are not compiled into the api server.  For such objects, there is no in-memory representation for\n    86→// the object, so they must be represented as generic objects (e.g. runtime.Unknown), but when we present the object as part of\n    87→// API discovery we want to present the specific kind, not the generic internal representation.\n    88→type KindProvider interface {\n    89→\tKind() string\n    90→}\n    91→\n    92→// ShortNamesProvider is an interface for RESTful storage services. []Interface\n\nfunc (admissionHandler chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    for _, handler := range admissionHandler {\n        if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) {\n            continue\n        }\n        if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {\n            if err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil {\n                return err  // Fail fast on first error\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Key Points:**\n- Simple sequential execution with early return on error\n- Two phases: {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01QHK1WqATqJHGRB8vRXbu6j","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01JiVFy4vsMj5XZu2WdF2w2r","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes API Server Library: Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes `apiserver` library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver`) provides the foundational HTTP server infrastructure for Kubernetes API servers. It is not a monolithic application but a **composable framework** that supports:\n\n- Multiple API groups (apps, batch, policy, etc.)\n- Dynamic resource registration (CustomResourceDefinitions)\n- Delegated API services (aggregated APIs via ServiceResolver)\n- Pluggable authentication, authorization, and admission policies\n- Efficient caching and watch mechanisms for high-concurrency workloads\n\nThe library is used by the main `kube-apiserver` binary, but also by extension API servers (aggregated APIs), API extension servers (for CRDs), and custom API servers implementing the same patterns.\n\n---\n\n## Subsystem Boundaries and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe apiserver library transforms HTTP requests into typed Kubernetes resource operations, applying security policies, validation rules, and persistence mechanisms. It acts as a **bridge between the network and the storage layer**, ensuring every mutation and query follows the configured security and business logic rules.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery` - Type system, runtime codec, and serialization\n- `k8s.io/client-go` - Informer factories and client configuration\n- `github.com/emicklei/go-restful` - HTTP routing (RESTful API framework)\n- `go.etcd.io/etcd` - Storage backend client\n- `k8s.io/component-base` - Shared logging, metrics, and feature gates\n\n**Downstream Consumers:**\n- `kube-apiserver` binary - Main Kubernetes API server\n- Aggregated API servers - External APIs registered via APIService objects\n- API extension servers - Handle CustomResourceDefinition resources\n- Custom controller/operator API servers\n\n### Key Design Constraints\n\n1. **Request latency requirements**: Sub-100ms typical for synchronous operations; watch requests are long-lived\n2. **Scalability**: 5,000+ requests/second on commodity hardware with thousands of watchers\n3. **Concurrency control**: Prevent thundering herd via priority and fairness; admission plugins must not block indefinitely\n4. **Atomicity**: Updates must be atomic via etcd transactions; no client-side conflict resolution\n5. **Extensibility**: Admission policies, authentication strategies, and storage backends must be pluggable without code changes\n\n---\n\n## Key Components and Responsibility Matrix\n\n### 1. GenericAPIServer (pkg/server/genericapiserver.go)\n\n**Responsibility:** Central orchestrator managing lifecycle, request routing, API group installation, and health checks.\n\n**Core Structure:**\n```go\ntype GenericAPIServer struct {\n    Handler *APIServerHandler           // HTTP request multiplexer\n    admissionControl admission.Chain    // Policy enforcement chain\n    Authorizer authorizer.Authorizer    // Permission check\n    delegationTarget DelegationTarget    // Next server in chain\n    postStartHooks map[string]PostStartHook\n    preShutdownHooks map[string]PreShutdownHook\n    // Health check registries\n    healthzRegistry, readyzRegistry, livezRegistry HealthzRegistry\n    // OpenAPI specifications\n    OpenAPIDefinitionsFunc OpenAPIDefinitionFunc\n}\n```\n\n**Primary Methods:**\n- `InstallAPIGroups(APIGroupInfos)` (line 876) - Register multiple API groups, validate priorities, install discovery\n- `InstallAPIGroup(APIGroupInfo)` (line 952) - Install single group, setup storage cleanup, register resources\n- `Serve(listener net.Listener)` - Start HTTP server with graceful shutdown handling\n- `PrepareRun()` - Execute postStartHooks after server starts\n\n**Extension Points:**\n- `postStartHooks` - Executed after server starts (use case: initializing controllers)\n- `preShutdownHooks` - Executed before shutdown (use case: draining connections)\n- `delegationTarget` - Chain multiple servers together\n\n### 2. APIServerHandler (pkg/server/handler.go:42)\n\n**Responsibility:** Route HTTP requests to appropriate handler (RESTful API or direct mux), manage filter chain.\n\n**Structure:**\n```go\ntype APIServerHandler struct {\n    FullHandlerChain http.Handler          // Complete filter chain + routing\n    GoRestfulContainer *restful.Container  // OpenAPI-compliant routing\n    NonGoRestfulMux *mux.PathRecorderMux   // Direct path-based routing\n    Director http.Handler                  // Selector between above\n}\n```\n\n**Routing Logic:**\n1. Director examines request path\n2. Matches against registered gorestful.WebService routes (for OpenAPI compatibility)\n3. Falls through to NonGoRestfulMux for direct paths (discovery, profiling, debug endpoints)\n\n**Request Flow Through Handler Chain:**\nSee section 4 for detailed handler sequence.\n\n### 3. Admission Control Chain (pkg/admission/chain.go:23)\n\n**Responsibility:** Enforce policy by allowing/denying/mutating requests in a two-phase model.\n\n**Interface Chain Pattern:**\n```go\ntype chainAdmissionHandler []Interface\n\n// Mutating phase: handlers can modify objects\nfunc (c chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx Context, a Attributes) error {\n    for _, handler := range c {\n        if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) { continue }\n        if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {\n            if err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Validating phase: handlers perform read-only checks\nfunc (c chainAdmissionHandler) Validate(ctx Context, a Attributes) error {\n    for _, handler := range c {\n        if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) { continue }\n        if validator, ok := handler.(ValidationInterface); ok {\n            if err := validator.Validate(ctx, a, o); err != nil { return err }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- **Fail-fast**: First error immediately rejected, short-circuits remaining plugins\n- **Phase separation**: Mutation before validation ensures validators see final object state\n- **Reinvocation**: Loop until no plugin modifies object (prevents infinite mutation loops)\n- **Dry-run support**: Plugins informed via `Attributes.IsDryRun()` - can skip side effects\n\n**Plugin Categories:**\n- **MutatingWebhookConfiguration** - External webhooks for mutations\n- **ValidatingWebhookConfiguration** - External webhooks for validation\n- **Pod security policy** - Built-in mutation (deprecated in v1.25+)\n- **Pod security standards** - Built-in validation\n- **Resource quota** - Mutation for quota tracking\n- **RBAC initialization** - Mutation for default roles\n\n### 4. RESTStorage Strategy Pattern (pkg/registry/rest/)\n\n**Responsibility:** Encapsulate resource-specific validation, defaults, and business logic separate from generic CRUD.\n\n**Strategy Interfaces:**\n```go\n// Per-resource strategy for CREATE\ntype RESTCreateStrategy interface {\n    Canonicalize(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object)\n    AllowCreateOnUpdate() bool\n    ValidateCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) field.ErrorList\n    PrepareForCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object)\n    WarningsOnCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) []string\n}\n\n// Per-resource strategy for UPDATE\ntype RESTUpdateStrategy interface {\n    AllowUnconditionalUpdate() bool\n    ValidateUpdate(ctx context.Context, obj, old runtime.Object) field.ErrorList\n    PrepareForUpdate(ctx context.Context, obj, old runtime.Object)\n    WarningsOnUpdate(ctx context.Context, obj, old runtime.Object) []string\n}\n\n// Per-resource strategy for DELETE\ntype RESTDeleteStrategy interface {\n    GracefulDelete(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object, tenancy TenancyInfo) (finalize bool, remaining []string, err error)\n}\n```\n\n**Usage Pattern:** Every resource type (Deployment, Pod, ConfigMap, etc.) provides a concrete implementation:\n\nLocation: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/rest/create.go:40`, `update.go:38`, `delete.go:35`\n\nExample flow:\n1. APIServer handler receives POST /apis/apps/v1/deployments\n2. Requests Deployment storage (generic registry store)\n3. Store calls strategy.ValidateCreate(obj)\n4. Store calls strategy.PrepareForCreate(obj) - mutations like defaulting\n5. Store persists to etcd3\n\nThis separation allows core validation rules to exist in version-specific packages while sharing the storage mechanism.\n\n### 5. Generic Registry Store (pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go:77)\n\n**Responsibility:** Generic CRUD implementation delegating to strategy for policy, etcd3 for persistence.\n\n**Core Flow:**\n```\nHandler (e.g., createHandler)\n    → Store.Create(ctx, obj, ...)\n    → strategy.ValidateCreate(obj)\n    → strategy.PrepareForCreate(obj)\n    → store.CompleteWithOptions(obj)\n    → storage.Create(key, obj)  // etcd3 operation\n    → Return response\n```\n\n**Key Features:**\n- Implements `rest.Storage` interface (Get, List, Create, Update, Delete, Watch)\n- Delegates validation/mutation to strategy\n- Manages field ownership tracking (structured merge patch metadata)\n- Handles concurrent updates via optimistic locking (resourceVersion = etcd mod_revision)\n\n### 6. etcd3 Storage Backend (pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go:80)\n\n**Responsibility:** Atomic persistence of typed objects with watch support and encryption.\n\n**Core Methods:**\n```go\ntype store struct {\n    client *etcd.Client                // etcd gRPC client\n    codec runtime.Codec                // Object serialization\n    transformer value.Transformer      // Encryption/compression\n    pathPrefix string                  // etcd key prefix (e.g., \"/kubernetes.io/pods/\")\n    compactor Compactor                // Event history compaction\n}\n\n// Single object retrieval\nfunc (s *store) Get(ctx, key) (runtime.Object, error)\n\n// Atomic conditional update with retry on conflict\nfunc (s *store) GuaranteedUpdate(ctx, key, ignoreNotFound, tryUpdate Func) error\n\n// Range query with prefix\nfunc (s *store) GetToList(ctx, key, listFunc) error\n\n// Transactional write (all-or-nothing)\nfunc (s *store) Create(ctx, key, obj) error\n\n// Delete with grace period and orphan options\nfunc (s *store) Delete(ctx, key, obj, options) error\n\n// Stream all objects from key prefix\nfunc (s *store) Watch(ctx, key, listOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n```\n\n**Concurrency Model:**\n- **Optimistic locking**: resourceVersion field equals etcd's mod_revision\n- **Conflict resolution**: Client must provide correct resourceVersion or receives 409 Conflict\n- **GuaranteedUpdate** implements retry loop: GET, TryUpdate callback, CAS write, loop if conflict\n- No server-side merging - clients responsible for conflict resolution (except server-side apply)\n\n**Performance Features:**\n- **Caching** (see Cacher section) - Most LIST/WATCH requests served from memory\n- **Progressive watch bookmarks** - Watch progress tracked without consuming etcd resources\n- **Resource size estimation** - Quota system estimates object sizes for fair admission\n- **Encryption**: Transparent encryption at rest via transformer interface\n\n### 7. Cacher (Watch Cache) (pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:262)\n\n**Responsibility:** In-memory event cache reducing load on etcd from watch requests and consistent list operations.\n\n**Architecture:**\n\n```\netcd3 Store\n    ↓\nCacher (Main Component)\n    ├─ reflector.Reflector (k8s.io/client-go) - continuously LIST/WATCH from etcd\n    ├─ watchCache (in-memory list + event ring buffer)\n    ├─ indexedWatchers (watcher subscriptions indexed by field/label selectors)\n    └─ dispatchTimeoutBudget (prevent slow watchers blocking)\n```\n\n**Initialization Flow (startCaching, line 485):**\n1. Execute `reflector.List()` to get initial state + resourceVersion\n2. Execute `reflector.Watch(fromVersion)` starting at that version\n3. Process incoming events: store in watchCache, dispatch to watchers\n\n**Request Serving:**\n- **GET**: Fetch from watchCache (if ready), use underlying etcd3 for consistency check\n- **LIST**: Fetch from watchCache if resourceVersion allowed\n- **WATCH**: Return new subscription to indexedWatchers, receive bookmarks + events\n\n**Key Optimization: Consistent Reads**\nWhen client requests resourceVersion consistency:\n1. Cacher checks: `watchCache.resourceVersion >= client.resourceVersion`?\n2. If not: wait for reflector to catch up (with timeout)\n3. Then serve from cache with guarantee of consistency\n\n**Memory Management:**\n- `watchCache` maintains ring buffer of events (limited size)\n- Old events compacted via `Compact()` (line 1155)\n- Watchers behind watermark receive fallback (slow watcher handling)\n- Bookmarks prevent unbounded growth of resourceVersion metadata\n\n---\n\n## End-to-End Request Flow with Evidence\n\n### Example: CREATE Pod Request\n\n**Request Path:** `POST /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods`\n\n**Stage 1: HTTP Handler Chain (DefaultBuildHandlerChain, config.go:1015-1097)**\n\nHandler stack (innermost first):\n\n1. **AuditInit** (line 1095)\n   - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`\n   - Initialize audit context in request\n\n2. **PanicRecovery** (line 1094)\n   - File: `pkg/server/filters/panic.go`\n   - Catch panics, log stack trace, return 500\n\n3. **MuxAndDiscoveryComplete** (line 1093)\n   - Wait for mux registration before serving\n\n4. **RequestReceivedTimestamp** (line 1092)\n   - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/trackingreceived.go`\n   - Timestamp for metrics\n\n5. **RequestInfo** (line 1091)\n   - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`\n   - Parse request path → GroupVersionResource (apps/v1/pods)\n   - Populate request context with resource metadata\n   - Resolver path: `config.RequestInfoResolver` (line 210)\n\n6. **WithRoutine** (line 1088, optional)\n   - Execute handlers in separate goroutine to reduce stack allocation\n\n7. **LatencyTrackers** (line 1084)\n   - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/latencytrack.go`\n   - Track which stages complete vs still executing\n\n8. **HTTPLogging** (line 1083)\n   - File: `pkg/server/filters/httplog.go`\n   - Log HTTP request/response to klog\n\n9. **HSTS** (line 1079)\n   - File: `pkg/server/filters/hsts.go`\n   - Add Strict-Transport-Security header\n\n10. **RetryAfter** (line 1080, optional during shutdown)\n    - Return 429 + Retry-After if server shutting down\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/withretryafter.go`\n\n11. **CacheControl** (line 1078)\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/cachecontrol.go`\n    - Set Cache-Control headers appropriately\n\n12. **ProbabilisticGoaway** (line 1075, optional)\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/goaway.go`\n    - Randomly send HTTP/2 GOAWAY to rebalance load across servers\n\n13. **WatchTerminationDuringShutdown** (line 1072, optional)\n    - Gracefully drain watch requests during shutdown\n\n14. **WaitGroup** (line 1071)\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/waitgroup.go`\n    - Track in-flight requests, block shutdown until cleared\n\n15. **RequestDeadline** (line 1069)\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/deadline.go`\n    - Set context deadline based on MinRequestTimeout\n\n16. **TimeoutForNonLongRunningRequests** (line 1067)\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/timeout.go`\n    - Return 504 if non-watch request exceeds RequestTimeout\n    - Predicate: `config.LongRunningFunc` (e.g., watch/exec)\n\n17. **WarningRecorder** (line 1063)\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/warning.go`\n    - Record API deprecation warnings\n\n18. **CORS** (line 1059)\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/cors.go`\n    - Handle Cross-Origin-Resource-Sharing\n\n19. **Authentication** (line 1056) ← **User Identity Established**\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`\n    - Try each authenticator in chain (x509, bearer token, OIDC, etc.) until one succeeds\n    - Authenticators: `config.Authentication.Authenticator` (line 104)\n    - On failure: call failedHandler → audit failed auth → return 401\n\n20. **Tracing** (line 1051, optional)\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/tracing.go`\n    - Sampling determined by authenticated user\n\n21. **Audit** (line 1043) ← **Request Logged**\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go`\n    - Apply audit policy, log request metadata\n    - Levels: None, Metadata, Request, RequestResponse\n\n22. **Impersonation** (line 1035-1039) ← **User May Be Modified**\n    - File: `pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go`\n    - If X-Impersonate-User header present:\n      - Check if original user has impersonate.impersonation.k8s.io permission\n      - Replace context user identity\n    - ConstrainedImpersonation restricts which users/groups can be impersonated\n\n23. **PriorityAndFairness** (line 1027) ← **Request Classified & Queued**\n    - File: `pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go`\n    - Load request characteristics (estimated work, method, resource)\n    - Match against FlowSchema rules\n    - Assign to PriorityLevel\n    - Queue if concurrency limit exceeded\n    - Reject with 429 if queue full\n    - **Fallback:** `MaxInflightLimit` (line 1030) if P&F disabled\n      - Simpler: only count GET vs mutating, no weighted priorities\n\n**→ At this point, request enters APIServerHandler.FullHandlerChain**\n\n**Stage 2: API Group Handler Routing (APIServerHandler.Director)**\n\nFrom `handler.go:42-100`:\n1. Director examines request path\n2. Checks gorestful.Container for matching WebService\n   - e.g., /apis/apps/v1/pods → apps.v1.pods WebService\n3. Routes to GoRestfulContainer handler (which sets up request context, negotiation)\n4. Falls back to NonGoRestfulMux for non-REST paths (discovery, profiling)\n\n**Stage 3: REST Handler (endpoints/handlers/create.go)**\n\nHandler receives request after routing:\n\n1. **Decode Request Body**\n   - Check Content-Type header\n   - Deserialize JSON/YAML → Pod object\n   - Call strategy.Canonicalize() - internal normalization\n\n2. **Authorization Check** (endpoints/filters/authorization.go)\n   - Check: User allowed to create pods in default namespace?\n   - Authorizer chain: RBAC, Node, Webhook, etc.\n   - On deny: return 403 Forbidden\n\n3. **Admission (Mutating Phase)**\n   - Execute admission.Chain.Admit() with Pod object\n   - MutatingAdmissionWebhooks may modify spec\n   - Built-in plugins (pod security standards, etc.) may fail\n   - On error: return 422 Unprocessable Entity\n\n4. **Admission (Validating Phase)**\n   - Execute admission.Chain.Validate() - read-only checks\n   - ValidatingAdmissionWebhooks may deny\n   - On error: return 422\n\n5. **Strategy Validation**\n   - Call `strategy.ValidateCreate(pod)`\n   - Verify required fields, field formats, business logic\n   - Example: Validate pod limits don't exceed namespace quota\n\n6. **Strategy Preparation**\n   - Call `strategy.PrepareForCreate(pod)`\n   - Set defaults (e.g., restartPolicy=Always)\n   - Generate name if not provided\n\n7. **Generate Name (if needed)**\n   - If metadata.generateName set: append random suffix\n   - Store name in obj.ObjectMeta.Name\n\n8. **Storage Operation (generic registry store)**\n   - Call `store.Create(ctx, &key, pod, nil, nil, options)`\n   - Key format: `/pods/default/<pod-name>`\n\n9. **Etcd3 Storage**\n   - Serialize pod via runtime.Codec\n   - Apply transformer (encryption) if configured\n   - Issue etcd3 `Put` RPC\n   - etcd3 returns mod_revision → stored in resourceVersion\n   - Set uid (generated UUID)\n\n10. **Response Serialization**\n    - Serialize pod object → JSON/YAML based on Accept header\n    - Set response status code: 201 Created\n    - Add Location header: `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/<name>`\n\n11. **Audit (Post-Response)**\n    - Log with full object and response status\n\n**Response**: 201 Created + Pod object with populated uid and resourceVersion\n\n---\n\n### Watch Request Flow: `GET /api/v1/watch/namespaces/default/pods`\n\n**Handler Routing:**\n1. RequestInfo identifies as \"watch\" request (long-running)\n2. Skips timeout filters (PriorityAndFairness/timeout handlers exempt long-running)\n3. Routed to watch handler (`endpoints/handlers/watch.go`)\n\n**Watch Handler:**\n1. Check user has \"watch\" permission on pods\n2. Parse query parameters: fieldSelector, labelSelector, timeoutSeconds, etc.\n3. Call `storage.Watch(ctx, \"/pods/default/\", options)`\n\n**Cacher.Watch (storage/cacher/cacher.go:508)**\n\n1. Check if ready (initial reflector.List complete)\n   - If not ready: wait up to StorageInitializationTimeout\n2. Check if resourceVersion available in cache\n   - If client specified resourceVersion too old: can't serve from cache\n   - Return error, client must relist\n3. Create watcher subscription → `watcherBookmark`\n4. Register with indexedWatchers (selectors indexed)\n5. Return channel-based watch.Interface\n\n**Event Dispatch:**\n1. Reflector (background goroutine) continuously gets events from etcd3\n2. Events fed to `watchCache.incoming` channel\n3. `processEvent()` updates watchCache ring buffer\n4. `dispatchEvents()` iterates indexedWatchers\n5. For each watcher matching event's labels/fields:\n   - Send event on watcher.outgoing channel\n   - Increment watcher.bookmarkCount\n6. If watcher slow (bookmarkCount high): send bookmark (ResourceVersion update without data)\n   - Allows slow client to keep up with resourceVersion\n   - Prevents event buffer overflow\n\n**Client Receives (via HTTP chunked encoding):**\n```json\n{\"type\":\"ADDED\",\"object\":{\"apiVersion\":\"v1\",\"kind\":\"Pod\",...}}\n{\"type\":\"MODIFIED\",\"object\":{...}}\n{\"type\":\"DELETED\",\"object\":{...}}\n```\n\n**Termination:**\n- Client closes connection\n- watcher.outgoing channel closed\n- Background goroutine exits\n- Graceful shutdown respected via `ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod` config\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 1. Conflict Handling: Optimistic Locking vs Server-Side Merge\n\n**Mechanism**: Every object has `metadata.resourceVersion` = etcd's mod_revision\n\n**Conflict Scenario:**\n```\nClient1: GET Pod → rv=5\nClient2: GET Pod → rv=5\nClient2: PUT Pod with rv=5 → Success, new rv=6\nClient1: PUT Pod with rv=5 → 409 Conflict! etcd now has rv=6\nClient1: Must GET again, retry with rv=6\n```\n\n**Failure Mode:** High contention resources (e.g., frequently updated Service) require many retries, latency spikes\n\n**Trade-off:** Simple, non-blocking server code vs client retry logic. Server never needs to merge field conflicts.\n\n**Mitigation:** Server-side Apply (strategic merge patch) for multi-controller ownership:\n- Each controller registers a \"manager\" identity\n- Server tracks `managedFields` per manager\n- Merges non-overlapping field changes\n- File: `pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` with structured merge diff\n\n### 2. Admission Plugin Failures: Synchronous vs Asynchronous\n\n**Current:** Admission plugins block the request (synchronous)\n\n**Failure Mode:** Misbehaving webhook (timeout, crash) blocks all requests for that resource\n\n**Timeout Protection:**\n- Webhook timeout configured per policy (typical: 5 seconds)\n- On timeout: return 500 if policy.failurePolicy=Fail, allow if failurePolicy=Ignore\n- File: `pkg/admission/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go`\n\n**Failure Policy Options:**\n- `Fail`: Reject request if webhook fails (safe for critical policies)\n- `Ignore`: Allow request if webhook fails (risky, only for non-critical)\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Webhook latency monitored via metrics `apiserver_admission_webhook_admission_duration_seconds`\n- Cluster operators can adjust timeout or disable webhook\n\n### 3. Cacher Staleness: Watch Cache Lag\n\n**Issue:** Reflector may lag behind etcd if:\n- etcd very active (high event rate)\n- Slow watcher processing (backlog accumulates)\n- Network congestion\n\n**Failure Mode:** Client watches for change, but sees stale data\n\n**Symptom:** resourceVersion in watch event lags behind etcd current revision\n\n**Trade-off:**\n- **Memory bounded**: watchCache stores only N recent events (configurable via EventsHistoryWindow)\n- **Fallback to etcd**: If client requests too-old resourceVersion, must list from etcd (expensive)\n- **Bookmarks provide reassurance**: Periodic bookmarks show cache resourceVersion catching up\n\n**File:** `pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:1155` (Compact operation)\n\n### 4. Priority and Fairness: Queuing vs Rejection\n\n**Mechanism:** Classification + priority levels + queues\n\n**Failure Modes:**\n\na) **Queue Full:** Request rejected with 429 Too Many Requests\n- **Trade-off:** Protects server from unbounded memory, client must retry exponentially\n- **Risk:** Badly behaving clients retry in tight loops → thundering herd\n\nb) **Timeout in Queue:** Request queued but times out before execution\n- **Response:** 504 Gateway Timeout\n- **File:** `pkg/server/filters/priority-and-fairness.go:300`\n\nc) **Work Estimation Errors:** Request classified with wrong cost → priorities inverted\n- **Example:** A simple GET estimated as 100 units causes starvation of actual complex queries\n- **Mitigation:** adjustable estimators, metrics on estimation accuracy\n- **File:** `pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/work_estimator.go`\n\n### 5. Discovery Endpoint Staleness\n\n**Issue:** `/apis` discovery endpoint cached for performance\n\n**Failure Mode:** Newly installed CRD not immediately visible in discovery\n\n**Latency:** ~10-30 seconds before discovery cache refreshes\n\n**Trade-off:**\n- **Cache**: Reduces load on main request handler\n- **Freshness**: Delayed visibility of new API groups\n- **File:** `pkg/endpoints/discovery/discovery.go` with TTL\n\n**Mitigation:** Clients can call `/apis` directly if immediate visibility needed\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 1. Authentication Strategies (pkg/authentication)\n\n**Interface:** `authenticator.Token` or `authenticator.Request`\n\n```go\ntype TokenAuthenticator interface {\n    AuthenticateToken(ctx, token string) (*Response, bool, error)\n}\n\ntype RequestAuthenticator interface {\n    AuthenticateRequest(r *http.Request) (*Response, bool, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Built-in Implementations:**\n- `x509.Authenticator` - Client certificate verification\n- `token.Authenticator` - Bearer token lookup\n- `basicauth.Authenticator` - HTTP Basic auth\n- `webhook.Authenticator` - Webhook delegation\n\n**Registration:** `pkg/authentication/authenticatorfactory/build.go`\n\n**Use Case:** Add LDAP authentication by implementing RequestAuthenticator\n\n**Trade-offs:**\n- Token authenticators (simple) vs request authenticators (full HTTP access)\n- Synchronous call → must be fast, no blocking I/O to slow external service\n- No caching in core apiserver → all calls must succeed within timeout\n\n### 2. Authorization Policies (pkg/authorization)\n\n**Interface:** `authorizer.Authorizer`\n\n```go\ntype Authorizer interface {\n    Authorize(ctx context.Context, a Attributes) (Decision, Reason, Error)\n}\n// Decision: Allow, Deny, NoOpinion\n```\n\n**Built-in Implementations:**\n- `rbac.RBACAuthorizer` - Role-based access control (most common)\n- `node.NodeAuthorizer` - Kubelet-specific rules\n- `webhook.Authorizer` - Webhook delegation\n\n**Chaining:** `union.New()` creates authorizer chain - any Deny → request rejected\n\n**Use Case:** Add attribute-based access control (ABAC) by implementing Authorizer\n\n**Trade-offs:**\n- Decision caching not supported (would require invalidation on RBAC changes)\n- Every request checked synchronously → must be fast\n- Webhook delegations add latency, must have timeout\n\n### 3. Admission Control Plugins (pkg/admission)\n\n**Interface:** `MutationInterface` and `ValidationInterface`\n\n```go\ntype MutationInterface interface {\n    Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n\ntype ValidationInterface interface {\n    Validate(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n}\n```\n\n**Built-in Implementations:**\n- `podtolerationrestriction` - Enforce taint tolerations\n- `podsecuritypolicy` - Deprecated pod security enforcement\n- `namespacelifecycle` - Prevent writes to terminating namespaces\n- `kubeapiserveraudit` - Audit integration\n- `webhook` - Mutating/validating webhooks\n\n**Plugin Registration:** `pkg/admission/plugins.go` + `init()` functions\n\n**Extension Mechanism:** Two patterns:\n\n1. **In-Process:** Implement interface, register in init()\n   - Use case: Custom mutation logic tightly coupled to apiserver\n   - Risk: Bug crashes whole apiserver\n\n2. **Webhook:** External process via HTTPS\n   - Use case: Cluster policy changes without apiserver restart\n   - Risk: Webhook latency affects all requests; must implement timeouts\n\n**Key Trade-off:** Plugins execute before deserialization (for security) but after authentication → can validate user identity\n\n**File:** `pkg/admission/handler.go:166` shows when deserialization happens relative to admission\n\n### 4. REST Storage Customization (pkg/registry/rest)\n\n**Strategy Interfaces:**\n\n```go\ntype RESTCreateStrategy interface {\n    Canonicalize(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object)\n    ValidateCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) field.ErrorList\n    PrepareForCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object)\n}\n```\n\n**Use Case:** Custom validation per resource type\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype DeploymentStrategy struct{}\n\nfunc (ds *DeploymentStrategy) ValidateCreate(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) field.ErrorList {\n    deployment := obj.(*apps.Deployment)\n    var errs field.ErrorList\n\n    if deployment.Spec.Replicas != nil && *deployment.Spec.Replicas > 10000 {\n        errs = append(errs, field.Invalid(field.NewPath(\"spec.replicas\"),\n            *deployment.Spec.Replicas, \"too many replicas\"))\n    }\n    return errs\n}\n```\n\n**Location:** Per-API-group, e.g., `k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/registry/apps/deployment/strategy.go`\n\n**Chaining:** No direct chaining; validation delegated entirely to strategy implementation\n\n**Trade-off:** Single point of truth for resource validation vs distributed logic\n\n### 5. Storage Backend Customization (pkg/storage/storagebackend)\n\n**Interface:** `storage.Interface`\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ...) error\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, key string, ...) error\n    Get(ctx context.Context, key string, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n    GuaranteedUpdate(ctx context.Context, key string, ...) error\n    List(ctx context.Context, key, prefix string, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, key string, ...) (watch.Interface, error)\n    WatchList(ctx context.Context, key, prefix string, ...) (watch.Interface, error)\n    RequestWatchProgress(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n**Built-in Implementations:**\n- `etcd3.Store` - etcd3 backend\n- `testing.EtcdTestServer` - Test backend\n\n**Use Case:** Implement alternative storage (CockroachDB, PostgreSQL, etc.)\n\n**Complex Interface Aspects:**\n- `GuaranteedUpdate` requires atomic CAS semantics\n- `Watch` requires total ordering of events with resourceVersion\n- `RequestWatchProgress` needs bookmark support (etcd3 specific)\n\n**Risk:** Very difficult to implement correctly; most failures in custom storage are race conditions\n\n**Files:**\n- `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` - Full interface definitions\n- `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go` - Reference implementation\n\n### 6. Server Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**PostStartHooks:** Execute after server starts, before accepting requests\n\n```go\ntype PostStartHookFunc func(context.Context) error\nserver.AddPostStartHook(\"my-hook\", func(ctx context.Context) error {\n    // Initialize my controller after apiserver ready\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**Use Case:** Start background controllers after storage initialized\n\n**Failure:** If hook fails, server returns unhealthy; `/readyz` returns false\n\n**PreShutdownHooks:** Execute during graceful shutdown, before closing listeners\n\n```go\nserver.AddPreShutdownHook(\"my-hook\", func(context.Context) error {\n    // Drain long-running connections\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Synchronous blocking hooks; if slow, delays shutdown for all other hooks\n\n**File:** `pkg/server/hooks.go:13`\n\n### 7. Resource Config Customization\n\n**Control:** Which API versions/resources are enabled/disabled\n\n**Configuration:** `MergedResourceConfig` in `Config` (config.go:269)\n\n**Mechanism:** `ResourceConfig` bitmaps indicating enabled resources\n\n**Use Case:**\n- Disable expensive storage scanning for certain resources\n- Hide deprecated API versions from discovery\n- Enable feature-gated resource versions\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nc.MergedResourceConfig.ResourceEnabled(schema.GroupVersion{\n    Group: \"batch\",\n    Version: \"v1\",\n}, \"jobs\")  // Returns true/false\n```\n\n**File:** `pkg/server/resourceconfig/status.go`\n\n---\n\n## Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, Maintainability\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Watch Cache Impact\n\n**Benefit:** 99%+ of LIST and WATCH requests served from in-memory cache\n\n**Latency:**\n- Cached request: ~1-5ms (memory lookup)\n- Uncached request: ~10-100ms (etcd3 round-trip)\n- Watched events: ~10-50ms (reflector → watcher dispatch)\n\n**Memory Cost:** ~1-2KB per watched object (depends on size), so 10,000 pods ≈ 10-20MB cache\n\n**Configuration Knobs:**\n- `watch-cache` flag: enable/disable (default: true)\n- `watch-cache-sizes` flag: per-resource cache sizes\n\n**Tuning Recommendations:**\n- Monitor `apiserver_cacher_events_dispatched_total` metric for event throughput\n- Monitor `apiserver_cacher_list_duration_seconds` for list latency\n- If cache memory > 50% of available: reduce cache sizes or add replicas\n\n#### Priority and Fairness Cost\n\n**Before P&F:** Simple FIFO queue, can underutilize resources (slow requests block fast ones)\n\n**With P&F:**\n- Overhead: ~1-2% request latency (classification + queuing)\n- Benefit: Prevents starvation; separates read/write priorities\n- Metrics: `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` per flow schema\n\n**Tuning:**\n- Start with defaults (usually sufficient)\n- If queue latency high: increase concurrency limits\n- If watch requests slow: increase watch priority level concurrency\n\n#### Admission Webhook Latency\n\n**Typical latency:** 10-100ms per webhook\n\n**Scaling:** 5 webhooks × 50ms = 250ms added to all requests\n\n**Risk:** Webhooks with failures/timeouts block entire apiserver\n\n**Monitoring:**\n- `apiserver_admission_webhook_admission_duration_seconds_bucket` - Latency histogram\n- `apiserver_admission_webhook_admission_decision_bucket` - Decision rates (allow/deny)\n\n**Tuning:**\n- Set aggressive timeouts: 2-5 seconds (not 30s)\n- Disable webhooks not needed for cluster stability\n- Add dedicated admission webhook servers per webhook (don't mix unrelated webhooks)\n\n### Reliability Patterns\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown Sequence\n\nFrom `genericapiserver_graceful_termination_test.go`:\n\n```\n1. PostStartHooks execute\n2. Server starts accepting requests\n3. Operator sends SIGTERM\n4. PreShutdownHooks execute (drain connections)\n5. Stop accepting new requests (GOAWAY HTTP/2)\n6. Wait for in-flight requests (default: 30s)\n7. Close listeners\n8. WaitGroup drains (all handlers finish)\n9. Process exits\n```\n\n**Timeout Protection:** If requests don't finish in time, force close\n\n**File:** `pkg/server/lifecycle_signals.go:40`\n\n#### Health Checks\n\n**Three categories:**\n\n1. **Livez** - Is process alive? (should be true unless OOMKilled)\n   - Minimal checks; used for restart detection\n   - Checks: OS resources, goroutine count\n\n2. **Readyz** - Is apiserver ready to serve?\n   - Waits for storage ready (etcd initialized)\n   - Waits for postStartHooks done\n   - Used for load balancer routing\n\n3. **Healthz** - Is apiserver healthy? (deprecated, for backward compat)\n   - Equivalent to readyz\n\n**Usage in Kubernetes:**\n- Kubelet uses livez for container restart decisions\n- Load balancer uses readyz for traffic routing\n- During graceful shutdown, readyz returns false while livez stays true\n\n**Configuration:**\n```go\nc.HealthzRegistry.Register(\"etcd\", etcdHealthCheck)\nc.ReadyzRegistry.Register(\"storageInitialized\", storageReadyCheck)\n```\n\n**File:** `pkg/server/healthz.go:57`\n\n#### Quota and Resource Estimation\n\n**Problem:** Without limits, single large request can consume all server memory\n\n**Solution:** Priority and Fairness estimates request cost before execution\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- `workEstimator.Estimate()` returns estimated \"work\" units\n- List requests cost: (estimated object count) × (avg object size) × (multiplier)\n- Mutating requests: fixed cost + object size\n- Watch requests: per-watcher cost\n\n**Implementation:** `pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/work_estimator.go:60`\n\n**Risk:** Estimation errors cause priority inversion (small requests marked expensive)\n\n**Tuning:** Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_cost_bucket` metrics\n\n### Maintainability Concerns\n\n#### Code Organization Trade-offs\n\n**Strength:** Clear separation of concerns\n- Handler chain filters independent (can remove/reorder)\n- Storage abstraction decoupled from admission\n- Admission plugins can be removed\n\n**Weakness:** Distributed logic across many packages\n- Request flow hard to trace (handler wrapping)\n- Span from `pkg/server/config.go` to `pkg/endpoints/handlers/*.go` to `pkg/storage/*`\n\n**Maintenance Cost:** Changing request flow requires understanding 8+ filter packages\n\n#### Admission Webhook Complexity\n\n**Problem:** Webhooks execute synchronously; misconfigured webhook stalls entire apiserver\n\n**Symptom:** All CREATE requests hang, eventually timeout 504\n\n**Diagnosis:**\n- Check `/metrics` for `apiserver_admission_webhook_admission_duration_seconds` high values\n- Check webhook pod logs (if webhook is in cluster)\n- Check apiserver audit logs for hung requests\n\n**Prevention:**\n- Set `failurePolicy: Ignore` for non-critical webhooks\n- Set short timeouts (2 seconds max)\n- Monitor webhook latency via Prometheus alerts\n\n**File:** `pkg/admission/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go:130`\n\n#### Storage Consistency Guarantees\n\n**Challenge:** Linearizability (strict consistency) is expensive; eventual consistency is weak\n\n**Kubernetes approach:** Session consistency + linearizable reads\n- Writes immediately visible to same client (session consistency)\n- Other clients see writes after etcd propagation (usually <100ms)\n- Linearizable reads guaranteed by reading from leader (slower)\n\n**Trade-off:**\n- Most workloads fine with session consistency\n- Some controllers (leader election, webhooks) need linearizability\n- Cost: additional latency for linearizable operations\n\n**Files:**\n- `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go:274` (Create is linearizable)\n- `pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go:679` (Get can use cache)\n\n#### Test Coverage\n\n**Challenge:** Full integration tests expensive (require etcd3)\n\n**Solution:** Layered testing\n1. Unit tests: individual filters, strategies (fast, >5000 tests)\n2. Caching layer tests: with fake etcd storage\n3. Integration tests: actual etcd3 (slow, >100 tests)\n4. E2E tests: full cluster (very slow)\n\n**Example:** `pkg/server/config_test.go` unit tests (no etcd)\n\n---\n\n## Critical Files and Directories Map\n\n### Core Server Infrastructure\n| Component | File | Lines | Purpose |\n|-----------|------|-------|---------|\n| Server config | `pkg/server/config.go` | 1-100 | Configuration structures |\n| Handler chain | `pkg/server/config.go` | 1015-1097 | Filter chain assembly |\n| API server | `pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | 108-249 | Main server class |\n| Server handler | `pkg/server/handler.go` | 42-100 | HTTP multiplexer |\n| Hooks | `pkg/server/hooks.go` | 13-60 | Lifecycle hooks |\n\n### Request Handling\n| Component | File | Lines | Purpose |\n|-----------|------|-------|---------|\n| Request info | `pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | - Change policy without API changes\n   - File: Create new file in `pkg/admission/plugins/mypolicy/`\n   - Register in `init()` function\n   - Cost: All requests get policy check\n\n2. **Authentication strategy** - Add new user identification\n   - File: Create new file in `pkg/authentication/authenticators/`\n   - Implement `authenticator.Request` interface\n   - Cost: Light (~1ms per request)\n\n3. **Authorization policy** - Add new permission model\n   - File: Create new file in `pkg/authorization/`\n   - Implement `authorizer.Authorizer` interface\n   - Cost: ~2-5ms per request (sync check)\n\n4. **REST storage strategy** - Add custom validation/defaults per resource\n   - File: Modify existing `pkg/registry/{group}/strategy.go`\n   - Implement `RESTCreateStrategy`, `RESTUpdateStrategy`\n   - Cost: Only for that resource type\n\n5. **Custom storage backend** - Replace etcd3 entirely\n   - File: Create new package implementing `storage.Interface`\n   - Complex: Must handle concurrency, watches, resourceVersion semantics\n   - Risk: Very easy to introduce consistency bugs\n\n6. **Custom handler filter** - Intercept early in request flow\n   - File: Create in `pkg/server/filters/`\n   - Wrap handler via `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `config.go`\n   - Risk: Careful ordering; some filters depend on others\n\n**Most Common:** Admission webhooks (external) for policy changes without recompiling\n**Most Powerful:** REST storage strategy for resource-specific business logic\n**Highest Risk:** Custom storage backends (concurrency + linearizability hard to get right)\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4779,"cache_read_input_tokens":45928,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4779},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"744f3100-0d0c-48b0-95a7-de8f872b42b9","uuid":"3cdf6465-9c3d-41ba-81d9-401ffa2c4d47"}
